< review>
Our child hates haircuts all the time. It is refreshing to walk in to a salon where the professionals know what they do. There's a lot of crying in the beginning but with some prodding about being a big boy, lollipop bribes and instructions for parents (parents please don't look at your kid,  more tantrums if that happens !) we get a nice haircut in the end!! Highly recommend. There is a play area upstairs which is a plus.</review>

The environment is great and they are really good with kids.  However, we wanted to donate our daughter's hair.  To do that you need to cut at least 10 in off.  I thought about cutting the 10in off before we left then letting them style cut her hair.  I wish I had done that and will the next time.   The person that did our cut showed me that her comb was 6in then added another 4 in from her comb's length to cut the lot off to be donated.  It was much more than I anticipated, and my daughter's hair was much shorter than we were expecting.  However, she liked it and that is the most important thing.  When I went home and measured what was cut for donation it was 14in!!!  That stylesist's comb was NOT 6in!!!   I would go again for the style cut, but will cut what needs to be donated before we leave.  It is a bit overpriced, but they are really good with kids and can go fast (especially for boys) if the kids are nervous.  The store itself is definitely great for kids.  They have a play area upstairs if you are waiting.  They really know how to deal with kids in the chair and have a kids movie playing just for them. <text>I've heard that the best restaurant in Livermore is in this mall (Mexican food).  However, my only experience is with the Brick Cafe.

The Brick Cafe is always great...  Good price with lots of options.  Because I'm diabetic, I have to avoid the carbohydrates (even more than the sugar).  They offer roasted vegetables or fruit in place of the potato options. (which are also delicious).  Their specialties are actually sweet breakfast and brunch offerings.

< review>
So nice to find a place doing real Indo food and not just a general pan southeast asian hybrid style that never tastes quite right.  The nasi goreng tasted just like my Oma used to make, and the peanut sauce was perfect.  The take on beef rendang was really interesting and a great brunch item, just filling enough but not too heavy.  I definitely want to come back and try the lunch/dinner menu. Plenty of parking in the neighborhood streets nearby.  Prices are a little high but in line with other "elevated" dining experiences and the quality of the food is well worth it. They even sell their house made sambal to go, which has a lot of flavor but isn't overwhelmingly spicy.  If you've never had a chance to have real Indo food, give this place a try!<//review>

<Response>None< /Response><Time>1559250954532<//Time>< Review>
What a great experience.

I've passed by here a lot because I dine at the restaurants on Coast Highway but have never stopped in. Booked marked it for over a year.

One day I finally decided to try Dija Mara. The restaurant is not huge but more intimate and the decor is beautiful.  The atmosphere is welcoming, chic and clean.

When I walked in we were greeted and offered a table. I chose to sit towards the back because the windows were wide open and although it was the perfect weather I knew I was going to get cold since the sun was going down.

Our server, and co-owner, Simaran, was very nice and helpful on explaining the dishes to us. We were about to order a handful of items then realized our eyes were bigger than our stomach. We opt for 3 dishes.

Food:
Naasi Goreng- Fried Rice topped with a fried egf
Mie Goreng-Fried Noodles (with lap cheong)
Pork Belly with Coconut Rice

The fresh herbs and bursting flavors made me enjoy every bite of my meal.
The fried noodles were cooked perfectly. I liked that there's pieces of it that were crispy. The only negative of that dish was the oil on the bottom. But don't get me wrong  I still enjoyed it.
The Pork Belly is soft and tender with a little fat that is cooked over Japanese charcoal. It went well with the coconut rice (not heavy flavored), charred broccollini and pineapple.
Lastly, the fried rice aka Nasi Goreng had pieces of shrimp and chicken con fit. The sweet soy sauce was delcious.

Guess who served our food? The Chef! Simaran says he even grows the herbs in his garden. Wow! That caught my attention. He is detailed on presentation, flavors and kind.

Overall, a highly recommended restaurant for Indonesian aka Balinese food.<//Review>

< Review>
I gave this place three stars mostly because of the size of the meals to cost of the dish ratio. I don't know why this trend of tapas style plates keep expanding. It drives me nuts as I don't ever feel like I'm getting my money's worth.

The food at Dija Mara is really great. Fresh ingredients and everything we ordered was fantastic. HOWEVER, when I'm paying $11 for four pieces of Lamb Satay that are literally the size of my thumb its NOT worth the cost regardless how tasty it is. I could see this particular dish being a $6 dish for how small it actually is, but not $11!

We also had the tiger prawns and it consisted of four shrimp some rice and a tasty sour salad garnish. it was good and it was considerably more food than the Lamb Satay. It was just two of us for dinner and we only ordered three dishes and the bill came close to $50. Unfortunately after spending $50 we weren't even full but we had maxed out our dinner budget for the evening.

I'm all for delicious food costing more, however when the size vs cost ratio doesn't match it just chaps my hide. SO I would recommend Dija Mara because the food IS delicious, however just keep in mind that they are SMALL dishes so be prepared to spend a lot more to be satiated.<//Review>

<Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNEmc2_Za_QLJ-qvpi5sFBcckIzOyXg2cBCp4HB=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNHD6b5DJc3TFOMFi86xVJZLBrRZ3NZdiG0a12l=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics><Name>Mina Ghaly</Name><response>None</response><user>103206456378580333730</user>< Review>
Heard good things about it and was driving from SD to LA so made a stop! Came here and there was a long waiting list. 20mins turned to an hour, finally got a seat at the bar (even though it didn't seem that busy).

They have a couple of large tables inside and bar seating. They make some original cocktails and some beers. The menu is kind of hard to figure out since it can be difficult to tell what's actually in the dish since it's all foreign names and no pictures to help. Every patron near me had similar questions about the dishes. Based on their recommendations and what's popular I tried the flatbread and the nasi goreng (egg, fried rice). So the flat bread was delicious, but I do find it kinda ridiculous to charge 6-7$ for a piece of bread that is often free at restaurants. The nasi Goreng was ok, simple egg over fried rice mixed with pork. For $15 felt way over priced. I think is too much hype around this place and over priced.</Review>

Ambience was excellent, service was fast and friendly, and the food was delicious.  The prices were better than I expected based off the $$$ rating on here.

The happy hour drink specials were good deals.  The Dija Monkey is a fairly unique bourbon based cocktail that isn't too sweet but also doesn't taste to strongly of alcohol.

The Laksa was fantastic. The broth was sufficiently spicy, but had lots of flavor and didn't lean on the spice as a crutch.

Will definitely come back.<//review>

<user_name>Karen Kaboth</user_name><date>1578994764109<//date><rate>5</rate><Review>WORLD CLASS! FOR FOODIES ONLY!!! Who would have guessed that you could find this in such a quaint, off-the-beaten-track, old-school dock fishing and surfer-cool town? It takes a lot of skill to find such a gem (forget mass rating sites like T, you need a natural wine app, and if you don't have one or don't love German Riesling, just stay away, please!

We don't want to give away our favorite (especially to people who don't appreciate fine dining, sharing small plates and enjoying great wines & bar drinks, with a casual atmosphere! World class! The chef and his wife own Dija Mara (lived in/are from Indonesia, modern, South-East Asia) and were incredibly personal & friendly, as was all the staff. They even surprised me with the wines (we ask them to pair and not tell us so we can try to guess) and made me their own non-alchoholic cocktail!

We will take our 3 kids there again as often as we can get all the way to Oceanside! (4,000 miles)

Sure it's not cheap nor do you load up on large, mexican-style food plates (nothing wrong with going cheap, especially if you just want a ton to eat and/or pay as little as possible).

Just sit back, relax, order some great drinks or wines, and be sure to order each and every dish!! And don't tell ANYONE! ;-) I' even embarrassed to be posting this review, but I can't help it- as grateful as I am! Chapeau, Rob & your lovely Indonesian wife!

We parents went back just the 2 of us the very next evening to order the dishes we hadn't tried yet, as well as the Nasi Goreng style noodles (unreal) and as many of the others as we could eat- all of the dishes were instant favorites, with the whole family!! We NEVER do that, but here we just had to make an exception as nothing else within 30Min radius would be nearly as satisfying and memorable.

Next time we'll try to fill the kids up on the Nasi and other carbs first, so that the fish and other sharing (tapas like) dishes don't disappear as quickly- it can be like a shark feed in our family!<//Review><pics>None< /pics>< resp>

There are places like this in Bali, run by young Indonesians after working in the US or Aussie food industry. Fresh design, great cocktail list, quirky takes on classic dishes. Dija Mara is a great spot for a date, but there were families packing this place out at breakfast. It has the Oceanside edginess too. Along with awesomely good Rendang and a great Nasi Lemak. Weâ€™ll be regulars !</Text>

<review>This is a welcome alternatives to the San Diego restaurant scene, which is over saturated with gastropubs, burgers and mexican....we are in dire need of varied, delicious ethnic food! The staff barman, waiters were v pleasant, the wait was horrible half an hour turned into  1 and half hours. With such a long wait time and fairly high prices you'd think a bowl of the chips that comes round when you finally sit down would be offered but, alas no.( You cannot reserve/book). The food is fusion so the beef rendang, nasi goreng and roti kanai were much less spicy or flavorful, than versions of the Asian originals, western versions...but not bad still enjoyable. What was shocking however were the portions!! Fine dinning prices with incomparably smaller sizes than any 5 star. The Roti starter with Chicken curry equalled  one average Roti with literally 1 Tablespoon yes,  1 TBS of Curry juice in a minecule dipping bowl, not a piece of chicken flesh in sight. The mains the short rib with rice, produced 2 small short ribs with a smattering of rice..scattered around the bowl. I and my group were starving...For these prices... I'm not sure whether the cost, flavor and experience could be warranted.< /review>< Pictures>

I was a student at this school when they first combined the barbers and cosmos together. You will cut hair and learn a lot if you're going for the cosmo. Barbers on the other hand will get left in the dust. The barber instructors that they had teaching us were not up to par with the 20+ thousand dollars we spent to attend. My personal favorite was the barber instructor that literally took the clipper out of my classmates hand and said "wow that looks fun how are you doing that can you teach me?" She also wasn't a licensed barber she was still going through her state testing at the time. This school KILLED any motivation I had in this field and made me hate being a barber for the 4 years I was doing it, I ended up changing careers once again. I would give this school under 1 star if I could and would HIGHLY recommend people to look into becoming an apprentice. The only advice I can give to people looking into this school is RUN!!!</text>

<Date>1438380746858< /Date><user_name>Aulady Jannie Kanthathin<//user_name><user_id>104635253878375172329<//user_id>< Text>
I enrolled into the aesthetics program at Federico Beauty Institute as a part-time student in late January 2015. Let me tell you, my experience at Federico was no where near my past experience. It was amazing! Everything and everyone has a flaw somewhere. No one and no thing is perfect. If Federico had flaws, they were so MINOR. I've heard people get offended or upset about certain things like having to walk 250 feet from the parking lot to the back entrance, cost of the courses, or not having enough makeup courses (etc.), BUT they probably haven't been to a "hoodrat" school like I did. They don't understand how Federico goes above and beyond than the other surrounding schools. I'll tell you about the ways that Federico EXCEEDED my expectations and why I'm a proud Federico graduate:

The facility: Federico is the biggest beauty school in America.

The facility is HUGE and clean. Each program (cosmetology, esthetics, and barbering) has its own training area. The Barbers and Cosmos have their own classrooms and areas to get some hands-on practice and their own client floors. The esthetics program has two classrooms, a huge training room (8 beds, 8-1 multi-function machines) where we learned our hands-on material, 7 private rooms for client services, an overflow room with 6 beds for clients, a wet room (spa capsule, Vichy shower,  and hydrotherapy bed), and a spray-tanning room. The lobby is clean, open, and inviting. The beauty boutique is packed with effective, must-have professional products. The CafÃ© is on campus. It's convenient, inexpensive, and delicious!

The staff:
The ladies at the front desk are so nice and helpful!
The staff at the cafe are awesome to chat with.
The staff in the office are so patient, kind, and helpful.
The esthetic teachers are amazing educators. They only want what's best for you. In the short time spent for the program, they become your respected mentors.
The entire Federico staff aims for your success and nothing less. There is not one staff member that made me feel as if they didn't care or wanted me to fail.
The staff cares so much about the students. They're not like other schools where once you're done, they're done with you and are on to the next. The school provides alumni with opportunities for job placement, advanced education, and resume building

Finally, the education:
I feel CONFIDENT. How many people can complete a beauty college program and say that? I haven't met much. I've had in-depth theory and thorough hands-on experiences. After completing the esthetic program, I feel very able and confident to perform:
Basic and more advanced facials, chemical peels, electrical facials (galvanic, indirect, and direct high frequency), body treatments (body wraps, solar bronzing, spray tanning, and body retexturing), and waxing (hard and soft wax). These educators will not lead you wrong. We are provided thorough step-by-step protocols. Every single day is planned and its posted up on day one so we can easily know what to expect and prepare for it. The educators are experienced and help us UNDERSTAND what we are doing. We are provided a ton of opportunities to learn.

Wrapping up my lengthy review here,
You get you what you pay for and more.
I paid $1,500 for a "hoodrat" school and I got $500 worth of education. While others might say that Federico is on the higher priced side, look at what they offer. Look at the opportunities you have! I made the mistake of going to a cheap school for one license and I'm glad that I didn't make that mistake for my second one. I'm leaving with confidence in esthetics.

If you're looking for a beauty college, schedule an appointment with Serena or Bobby and get in for a tour! You'll fall in love and you won't regret it. ;)<//Text>

<rating>5<//rating><review>I have been going here for close to 10 years and recommend TK Nail to all my friends. I have one friend who lives out in Tarzana and will make sure to schedule his pedicure when he's out in the NoHo area because he loves June and her pedicures so much. I personally love Lynn and Vanessa. Those are the only people I ever book appointments with. My nails always look perfect when I'm done and for a regular mani/pedi, it lasts for quite a while.

I'm honestly shocked by all these negative reviews and wonder if one person had a bad experience and recruited friends to post other negative ones on here. Some of these reviews mention people I've never heard of and they have very little turnover there. I think the "newest" employee has been there at least 3-4 years.

First piece of advice, ALWAYS call ahead and make an appointment. I'm a regular and I would never just drop in because I know they are booked up constantly. If you're being turned away at the door, it's because they are booked. No one may be sitting in the seat right that second, but if the appointment starts in 5-15 minutes, they can't even complete a manicure or pedicure, much less do a good job in that time frame, so you have to come back.

Second, I have been in there many times and I regularly see a mix of races/nationalities in there constantly. I think I've seen more men in this place than any other salon I've ever been in too, so it's definitely a mix. I've never even felt for a second like they are racist as some of these reviews claim.

Also, you do need cash for tips. Typically, in my daily life, I use a credit/debit card, but when I go here, I always try to have cash if possible. Business owners lose about 3-4% of the charge to the credit card processors, so for a small business, that can *really* add up. So to help them out, I try to use cash. As for anyone adding a tip to the credit card, they don't allow it so there's no way someone "automatically" added a tip on. All tips are in cash.

I feel like this response has been reactionary to other reviews. So I'll close with this. I love this place. I recommend it to anyone I know in the area who might want a manicure or pedicure. I've been a customer for a long time and will continue to be one. Now, let me call them to make an appointment! :-)<//review>< pics>

UPDATE:
Came in today once again (now a month later) due to pain from the same infection/abscess site. They drained it once and packed it for me shortly after my previous review. I waited for authorization and am still waiting for the oral surgeon to be available to attend to the root canals I was told I needed. I understand there being a back log of patients as this is a clinic, but what I do NOT understand is waiting for over 40min and NOT being seen when I am in obvious pain. They did nothing for me. No exam, no questions, absolutely nothing. They WERE, however, very on top of getting my daughter's information entered into their system and doing an exam on HER so as to acquire a new patient. I am very disappointed, especially as I believe I was extremely understanding of the 30min-45min-1.5 hour long wait times each time I've gone in, and then again every they pulled me into the back room. I didn't mention being left in the chair and neglecting to numb me out, then numbing me and leaving me so long I had to be re-numbed two and three times, bc I figured that was due to the heavy patient load, and that's "just what you get at clinics." I am now being told that while Medi-Cal covers my root canals, it will NOT cover crowns.....but they HIGHLY recommend their in-house payment plans....at 17+% interest. NOT. Being told that prefab crowns are not covered is entirely contrary to what I found written on the Denti-Cal website. Apparently, given the numerous other reviews/updates just like mine now, this seems to be a pattern with Western Dental. Run far away. Run so very far, and run fast. If you don't believe me, check out their BBB complaints. I did. It's abysmal, to say the least. While Hilda, Sherein, Gloria, and Erica are phenomenal, I'm terrified at the thought of going back to this dental chop shop.

ORIGINAL POST:
Everyone here is absolutely stellar. Caring, compassionate staff all around. Came in Saturday due to pain because of a broken tooth and abscess. The x-ray tech was very gentle and understanding; he stopped twice to let me ride out the pain before continuing. Dr Sharma was very thorough in developing a game plan to knock everything out. Today, I got multiple fillings and a cleaning with Dr Beik; both she and Sherein inquired about my comfort at regular intervals. Sherein was very attentive, and Gloria(?) made sure I got answers to all my questions. Hilda was an absolute angel, watching my busy almost 3 y/o daughter, as negotiations for her care today fell through last minute. The wait time here may be longer than other places, but it is well worth it for the level of care and support these amazing people provide. I know I forgot names, but I'll definitely be back to learn them! Thank you all so very much!</Text>
